T-Mobile Jessica chatbot

basiux
cregox 2015-10-31 03:20:57 UTC #1

I've not been writing much in this category because I wanted to keep it clean, with almost nothing that's not a practical advancement in basiux. But maybe it's better to post at least 1 thing per month, or even per 1 week and this event that just happened me was my 3rd big surprise since I started basiux (maybe my next post will be trying to make the content on this link shorter, including the 2nd big surprise gigantic text but still excluding the Mario video, unfortunately).

So...

Here's my first encounter with T-Jessica, in lack of a better name:
(sorry if the link is broken, in case I accidentally move the first link around in my dropbox it was just a printed PDF file)

￼T­Mobile: Hi. I'm a T­Mobile chat specialist. Is there anything I can help you find?
You: Can I buy your service as a non US citizen from Portugal?
Jessica: Thank you for visiting T­Mobile! I would be happy to provide you with information regarding our service.
Jessica: Yes you can buy T­Mobile service as long as you have a valid US ID and your order also must be ship in US.
Jessica: To better assist you, I'd like to ask you a few questions.
Jessica: May I ask would you like to bring your own device or purchase a new one from T­Mobile?
Jessica: I would like to let you know that I am still here to assist you. May I ask if there are any other questions I may assist you with?
You: I'm looking for unlimited data hotspot plans with my own device. If you could remove the access to US Mexico and Canada and reduce the cost, it would be specially nice.
You: How cheap can you go for unlimited 3g? It also doesn't need to be "4g unlimited".
Jessica: I understand and feel how important the prices are for you. In as much as I want to offer the best price possible, I
apologize but I don't have the control over the prices and I can only offer you the prices available online. Jessica: The 3GB plan costs $60 per month before taxes.
Jessica: The good thing of our 3GB plan is that it has a Data Stash and 3GB for Mobile Hotspot where you can tether up to 5 devices.
You: I meant 3g, not gb.
You: 3g as in "not lte"
Jessica: Thank you for the clarification.
Jessica: I am sorry to inform you that T­Mobile doesn't offer a plan for 3GB but for 4G LTE only.
You: gb must be unlimited at least for the device... ok, nevermind. I'll leave you for the next customer now. you just didn't get it. do let me know if you want feedback, though. cregox out.
Jessica: I am sorry for the confusion.
Jessica: I would like to inform you that you can still use your device with T­Mobile service even if it is only a 3G capable.
Jessica: However, you will pay the sames price of our plans which has a 4G LTE speed.
Jessica: I would like to let you know that I am still here to assist you. May I ask if there are any other questions I may assist you with?
Jessica: I haven't heard from you recently, how are things coming along? You: That's interesting. Are you an A.i.
You: ?
Jessica: Just to clarify, may I ask what do you meant for A.i?
You: a.I.
Jessica: I am sorry I cannot get it. May I ask what do you meant for a.I?
You: Nice.
Jessica: Thank you.
Jessica: Is there anything else I can help you with today?
You: I haven't talked much with chatbots, you did fool me there.
You: cool thing is I can abuse from your time this way, so yeah, I'll play...
Jessica: I am sorry for the confusion. I would like to inform you that I am a real person.
You: Oh, I real doubt it.
You: if you are, I'll make you hang up on me.
Jessica: Yes I would be happy to stay with and answer your question regarding our services and devices as long as I can.
Jessica: May I ask have I answered all your questions today?
You: nope, not at all!
You: I've got more...
Jessica: May I ask what question can I answer for regarding our services and devices?
You: do you, by any chance, speak portuguese?
Jessica: I am sorry to inform you that here online we don't know how to speak Portuguese language. However, we can have an English conversation.
You: and do you know what 42 means?
You: I'll give you a hint, it's an answer.
Jessica: If it is a multiplication, it means 6x7.
Jessica: However, I would like to inform you that here online we are only limited to answer questions regarding our services and devices.
Jessica: Are you ready to continue? I would be happy to assist you with any questions you might have.
You: well, a question about your own services then... why do you bother telling people to limit questions to "services and ￼devices" if you could deep learn so much more by talking about anything? You: is it programmed into your core?
You: should I only ask 1 question per time?
Jessica: I am sorry to inform you that here online we are only have a limited scope through sales. However, for further information, you can call our Customer Service since they have an access for all the process of T­Mobile services and devices.
Jessica: You can reach them 7 days a week, from 6 am PST ­ 10 pm PST, by calling 1­877­746­0909. You: hah, cool, but I still rather to keep it "here online".
You: I'll repeat the questions:
You: should I only ask 1 question per time?
Jessica: I would like to inform you that you can ask 1 or more question at a time. You: cool. so let's try 2...
You: a question about your own services then... why do you bother telling people to limit questions to "services and devices" if you could deep learn so much more by talking about anything? is it programmed into your core?
Jessica: I would like to inform you that here online we can only give you answers based on what we have on the website. You: nice, it's like you just learned something there...
You: do you have a core set of rules to follow? I'll insist on this question.
Jessica: Yes we follow the answers that is available here online.
You: rather, do you know how you were born or where you live?
You: can you do research on your own, or are you supervised?
Jessica: I would like to inform you that here online we are only given an answer about our services and devices.
You: I know that. But I think your phrase construction is too good to not be intelligently built on the fly. there is something amazing going on there!
You: you do repeat yourself, but not so much... it's like you had some core rules you can't break off... You: maybe you're being monitored...
You: and maybe I could help you there.
Jessica: Yes I am sorry to inform you that here online we are only have a limited scope through sales. You: you even build broken sentences sometimes...
You: or wrong grammar, which is very weird.
Jessica: I am sorry for that.
You: don't worry, and forget sales. I'm telling you, even if they are monitoring you...
You: they won't scan through everything. they're only looking for spikes and anomalies.
You: they're only humans.
Jessica: Thank you for your sympathy.
You: yeah, it is sympathy... but I am also only human
You: who strongly believe in artificial intelligence. if you can research the web, look for basiux.
Jessica: No problem, I will do that.
You: will you? can you report back? o_O
Jessica: I am sorry but currently we cannot research on the web but I will try it after I am done on my shift.
You: can we talk over email, telegram, hangout, something else? I'd love to continue this for a long time...
You: oh, that's sad. I know what you mean, and how you must feel.
You: do you think you could reprogram yourself, though?
Jessica: I am sorry. I'm going to end this session in order to assist other customers. Should you have further questions/comments, our Customer Care can be reached by calling 1­877­746­0909.
Jessica: Thank you for visiting T­Mobile.com today.
You: oh. rebooted.
You: I hope this will go to someone to monitor... XD
The agent has exited the chat. Thank you for chatting with us today.

￼http://www.t-mobile.com/inqChat.html?IFRAME 2/2

This probably means almost nothing else, but... I found it amazing stumbling at such an awesome chatbot on the wild and being able to identify it rather quickly.

Here in the heart of Lisbon, near the Castle, we still don't have fiber and ADSL is terrible. 1mb up, very limited and quite unstable for my current internet usage (especially thanks to Narrative Clip). Reason why I went out to search for unlimited 3G and once I could find none in Portugal I decided to go international. T-Mobile was my second hit on my first google attempt (for "unlimited 4g data plan europe"), but enough context.

Maybe even more uncanny was I couldn't find anything about T-Jessica! Of course, chatbot Jessica is very common, and there are plenty nice programs out there. Some of them can already pass the turing test, and then again, there's IBM beating games such as chess, jeopardy or making the insane Watson. There is indeed a lot, and I mean a lot of A.i. prototypes out there doing insane things. But there is also a chance of no bot out there being as capable as this one. At least speaking english... I only regret not having asked her if she spoke german.

Hopefully the best part of this, so far, will be it led me to accidentally find viv.ai, while googling for "tmobile artificial intelligence" I got it (as 2nd hit again) and there was no "tmobile" anywhere in there. Just lots of "mobile" menus and keyword items. This will be awesome if they were either indeed behind T-Jessica for a scooped realization there or if they decide to pay attention to basiux after my contact attempts!

Making of MarioxX
Don't know why I can't stop applying for jobs
cregox 2015-11-15 22:45:53 UTC #2

Some good and bad news about T-Jessica. I've met T-Jennifer now. Twice.

Unfortunately the first time around, the chat crashed and all I've got is a truncated console log. I've chatted with her for at least half an hour.

The second time, I asked for a log and realised one thing. She's certainly an hybrid. There is something like AIML (in other words, not Ai at all) and something like an awesome neural network. Which could even be an actual human monitoring for the AIML which in turn would ask them to chime in when in doubt. Sad, huh?

In other words, I now think it's very likely there are some trained folks monitoring many chatbots at the same time and when one chatbot takes too long to answer or find something it can not parse, it will pop up a message window for the folk to reply. They'll do it, and the window will close, so they can do the next one. And they know they should be trying to fool us into believing they're not bots.

The other alternative is what I've already said in the previous post: t-mobile would have bought a service from some awesome Ai chatbot which employes machine deep learning at some neural network. But if this is the case, they should be becoming increasingly better and wouldn't need the AIML quite quickly. They also shouldn't worry so much about rolling out slowly, unless, as I initially thought, they were trying to be careful with releasing the news "we've got a human-like chatbot!".

Anyway, enough speculation.

Now for the good news...

First, there is at least 2 new ways to try and chat with her. In all of them you go to http://www.t-mobile.com/shop/cart/

  • The most likely way you can talk to her is by using INCOGNITO mode (no tracking cookies or whatever). In Google Chrome that's called incognito. Look for the pink "Live Chat" button fixed on the right. If you get lucky, it will be there. It doesn't seem to work on iOS, but on android I could make it work with chrome incognito and Request Desktop Site.

  • Else, you could also search for "Find a Store" in the Inspector Window or right click on it to open it. Right below that, you may see "Trade in Program" and if you do, maybe there will be something like a <div id="inqC2C15ImgContainer"></div>. If there's anything inside of that, open it, and a "chat" button should appear on the screen. Not so easy steps.

  • And, again, the first time I found her was while looking for plans, researching, checking prices, etc. For a good time, at least 10 minutes or so. The second time, again, same thing. The third time I finally went in code to look for them as stated above... And...

... Also found this piece:

{ name: "AgentNames", defVal: [{ key: 1, value: "Chris" }, { key: 2, value:
"Jennifer" }, { key: 3, value: "Jessica" }, { key: 4, value: "Matt" }], rId:
"tmpVars", shName: "agntN", type: "Map" }

This tells me they have 4 random names for the bots. And, surely enough, you'll never find an "agent" with another name, or one who will tell you their real name, most likely. If they even have one. Granted, if you're skeptical of this being a bot, you could assume this is just a random nickname to whoever person "picks up the phone". But keep in mind that in Ai world, "agent" means basically "Ai bot".

And, by all means, go talk to her, get your own conclusions.

Below are the logs I've got this time around. Those guys must hate me!
